  <span id="freeText6112311790987187124" style="display:none">Deadly Little Games is the third book in the Touch Series by Laurie Faria Stolarz. Haven't read the first book? Why you be reading this review?! Go grab yourself a copy of Deadly Little Secret and let the fun times begin. fin. ;)<br /><br />I absolutely love Ms. Stolarz writing style. It's quick. It's snarky. It's creepy. It's awesome. <br /><br />I did feel the love-triangle introduced in this novel was a tad bit of a wth?. Firstly, the new "love" interest was the bad guy in the last novel, secondly, in my humble opinion, no boy could compete with Ben who can "touch-a-touch-a-touch-a-touch-a-me" any day of the week. Did I just go there? Sure did. <br /><br />Overall, I did enjoy this book, had my heart ripped out by the ending, and am hopeful that it will be patched up in the next novel.<br /><br />*crosses fingers*<br /><br />If you like a good mystery with a side of paranormal, and a hottie on a bike this be the book for you. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151504679" />
    <a title="Laura (Booksforbreakfast)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3936334-laura-booksforbreakfast"><img alt="Laura (Booksforbreakfast)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435104587p2/3936334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151504679?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura (Booksforbreakfast)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura (Booksforbreakfast)" href="/user/show/3936334-laura-booksforbreakfast">Laura (Booksforbreakfast)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151504679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7770464102528828384">I have really enjoyed the Touch series and this novel is no exception. There were some things I didn't care for, but overall, this book is a must read if you like paranormal romances.<br/><br/>The writing was great, as it always has been. I feel like the characters got a little more depth with them as they mature in the series. I have to say though, Wes and Kimmie totally stole the show away from Camelia and Ben in my opinion. They are SO funny and so imperfectly perfect that I want to put them in my pock</span>
  <span id="freeText7770464102528828384" style="display:none">I have really enjoyed the Touch series and this novel is no exception. There were some things I didn't care for, but overall, this book is a must read if you like paranormal romances.<br /><br />The writing was great, as it always has been. I feel like the characters got a little more depth with them as they mature in the series. I have to say though, Wes and Kimmie totally stole the show away from Camelia and Ben in my opinion. They are SO funny and so imperfectly perfect that I want to put them in my pocket.<br /><br />The suspense was really good as well. Though I did have an inkling as to whodunit, I thought the audio transcriptions and crosswords were very clever and a good way to keep the reader going. <br /><br />The ending was a little cheesy for me, and predictable, but I still am looking forward to Deadly Little Voices, due to come in November of 2011.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7770464102528828384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Some a bit more predictable than others. This particular book definitely tested my problem solving skills.   <span id="freeText8190811668624762058" style="display:none">This entire series has been one long guessing game for me. Each book brings to the table a new mystery with tons of twists and turns. Some a bit more predictable than others. This particular book definitely tested my problem solving skills. I had my theories from the beginning and then I switched them up half way through...and then I changed my mind again...only to be completely surprised at the end!!! I didn't see that coming at all! Or did I! OMG it was all there right in front of my face all along!! Indeed a clever little mystery you've created Laurie Faria Stolarz! Props to you! This was a truly great read. I loved the mystery. The characters themselves are simply amazing. And the downright cleverness deserves praise all it's own! Good job! Really good job! 5 stars from me! Bring on Deadly Little Voices! I can't wait to read it! </span>

I'll probably read the fourth book, because I'm a sucker for series', but I </span>

It was just too much. What are the chances that anyone would be associated with three different stalkers, much less in one year?! I'll probably read the fourth book, because I'm a sucker for series', but I sincerely hope Stolarz creates an original storyline instead of recycling the same one for the fourth time.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8644003977597541930">The concept of this series is great: a boy and a girl who can sense things supernaturally through touch and art. However, this is the third book in the series and each novel is basically the same. All three books consist of someone being stalked, and Camelia and Ben working on their relationship. That's about it. I was hoping for a fresh idea or at least some interesting new characters, but I was disappointed. I'm surprised Stolarz is even writing a fourth book, <i>Deadly Little Voices</i>. I would bet</span>
  <span id="freeText8644003977597541930" style="display:none">The concept of this series is great: a boy and a girl who can sense things supernaturally through touch and art. However, this is the third book in the series and each novel is basically the same. All three books consist of someone being stalked, and Camelia and Ben working on their relationship. That's about it. I was hoping for a fresh idea or at least some interesting new characters, but I was disappointed. I'm surprised Stolarz is even writing a fourth book, <i>Deadly Little Voices</i>. I would bet anything it contains the same old plot lines. However, I will admit I am mildly interested in Camelia's Aunt Alexia, but we'll see how it all plays out. Even though I'm no longer enjoying the touch novels, I'll read the next one. Otherwise I've gone this far for nothing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8644003977597541930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LJrLz6EBdQX2xrQGSEo1NCK5Ix2CVFauGVeYTyDZQ97YazfbfUrjx/PW+prRjRbKQeoQkPbfh/XZPLpqdgYldA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer6125801483219032923">Laurie Faria Stolarz grew up in Salem, MA, attended Merrimack College, and received an MFA in Creative Writing from Emerson College in Boston. <br/><br/>Laurie Faria Stolarz is an American author of young adult fiction novels, best known for her Blue is for Nightmares series. Her works, which feature teenage protagonists, blend elements found in mystery and romance novels.<br/><br/>Stolarz found sales success with he</span>
  <span id="freeText6125801483219032923" style="display:none">Laurie Faria Stolarz grew up in Salem, MA, attended Merrimack College, and received an MFA in Creative Writing from Emerson College in Boston. <br /><br />Laurie Faria Stolarz is an American author of young adult fiction novels, best known for her Blue is for Nightmares series. Her works, which feature teenage protagonists, blend elements found in mystery and romance novels.<br /><br />Stolarz found sales success with her first novel, Blue is for Nightmares, and followed it up with three more titles in the series, White is for Magic, Silver is for Secrets, and Red is for Remembrance, as well as a companion graphic novel, Black is for Beginnings. Stolarz is also the author of the Touch series (Deadly Little Secret, Deadly Little Lies, Deadly Little Games, Deadly Little Voices, and Deadly Little Lessons), as well as Bleed and Project 17. With more than two million books sold worldwide, Stolarz's titles have been named on various awards list. </span>
